Très habiles au javelot, ils affaiblissent les unités ennemies et brisent leurs formations, mais combattent aussi au corps à corps si la situation l'exige.

{Akinjis_descr_short}	Cavaliers légers utilisés comme mercenaires par les forces musulmanes. Ne portant pas d'armure afin d'aller plus vite, ces combattants sont armés d'un arc.
{Akinjis_descr}	Qualité : Moyenne.\nType : Mercenaire (entretien élevé, moral et discipline souvent légèrement réduits).\n\nLe terme "akinji" signifie "attaquants" et désigne des cavaliers légers servant dans les armées musulmanes. L'absence d'armure accroît leur vitesse. Armés d'un arc, ils peuvent utiliser une tactique de tir en cercle pour tenir l'ennemi sous un tir constant. Ils sont utiles pour harceler le flanc et les archers ennemis, mais dans une mêlée, ils se débanderont rapidement.

{Al_Haqa_Infantry_descr_short}	Ces troupes de qualité comprennent des Egyptiens, des Arabes et des fils de mamelouks. Ils sont équipés d'une bonne armure, d'un bouclier et d'un cimeterre.
{Al_Haqa_Infantry_descr}	Qualité : Supérieure.\nType : Professionnel de période avancée (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nLes Al-Haqas sont des Egyptiens et des Arabes, ainsi que des fils de mamelouks. Les Egyptiens et les Arabes ne sont pas autorisés à devenir des mamelouks. Quant aux fils de mamelouks, ils sont considérés comme des inférieurs, car à l'inverse des 'vrai turcs', ils ne sont pas nés sur les steppes. Néanmoins, les Al-Haqas sont des troupes importantes, souvent au service de leur émir, qui se battent aux côtés des mamelouks.

Ils ont combattu l'Empire byzantin, et leur ancien ennemi les apprécie désormais comme mercenaires. {Alforrats_descr_short}	Equipés d'une cotte de maille légère et d'une lance, cette unité est pratique pour flanquer votre ennemi et abattre les archers.
{Alforrats_descr}	Qualité : Milice.\nType : Local (manque d'entraînement, faible discipline et moral bas).\n\nLes Alforrats sont une cavalerie légère initialement utilisée comme une force de reconnaissance armée. Comme leur nom l'indique, ce sont des cavaliers "couverts", c'est-à-dire couverts de cuir clouté et d'une cotte de mailles légère comme principale armure. Ils sont bien entraînés, rapides et déterminés. Bien que manquant des montures massives de la cavalerie lourde, ils peuvent tout de même écraser les plus faibles unités d'infanterie grâce à la vitesse de leurs chevaux légers. Ils sont idéaux pour les embuscades, le débordement des unités déjà engagées ou l'attaque de l'infanterie légère.
{Alforrats}	Alforrats

Elle est lente à recharger et n'a pas la portée d'un arc long, mais sa puissance de feu est supérieure. Elle tire aussi des boulets enflammés enroulés dans des haillons enduits de poix afin de brûler l'adversaire, mais avec moins de précision.

{Hand_Gunners_descr}	Qualité : Supérieure (Combinaison).\nType : Professionnel urbain (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nCette unité manie la première arme à feu portative. Acritae were some of the most common troops throughout the Empire and were usually armed with heavy javelins(martiuvarbulus),swords and padded or chain mail armour.

{Cavalarii}	Cavalarii
{Cavalarii_descr_short}	Mounted archers armed with a composite bow, sword and shield.
{Cavalarii_descr}	(Καβαλάριοι).\n\nQualité : Moyenne.\nType : Professionnel de première période.\n\nSimply meaning “horsemen”, Cavalarii is a generic name for cavalry serving in the Empire’s armies. Up until the early medieval period cavalry, such as this were used to directly charge enemy lines. However, the development of heavier armoured cavalry and the recruitment of turkopuli (troops of mixed greek/turkish heritage) changed the role that Cavalarii played to that of mounted archers, taking advantage of the turkopoles’ skills in the saddle. They were armed with a composite bow, sword and a round shield.

{Contaratoi_descr_short}	Basic militia unit armed with spear and shield.
{Contaratoi_descr}	(Κονταράτοι).\n\nQualité : Milice.\nType : Milice urbaine (entretien nul dans les villes, moral réduit dans sur les champs de bataille).\n\nTheir name is derived from the Greek word for spear (kontos or kontarion). Contaratoi are the basic militia infantry unit of each thema (province) of the Empire. They make up the majority of each province’s armed forces. While not completely untrained, Contaratoi are still inferior to other, more professional units such as the Scoutatoi. Unlike the more professional units of the provincial armies they often use a larger variety of armour types, from cloth, to padded and even some chain mail Contaratoi are provided with a spear, shield and a metal helmet.

As mercenaries they often employed the latest weaponry. The newly developed handguns and arquebuses were no exception.
{Latinikon_descr_short}	Western European cavalry fighting for the Byzantine Empire. Armed with lances and swords.
{Latinikon_descr}	(Λατινικόν)\n\nQualité : Supérieure.\nType : Mercenaire (entretien élevé, moral et discipline souvent légèrement réduits).\n\nSince the time of Justinian and the Roman reconquista of Italy many European warriors offered their military service to the Byzantine Empire. These included Franks, Goths and Lombards. However the most well-known Latinikon were the Norman knights that entered the Empire’s service after the first Romano/Norman war in Italy. These Norman knights brought to the Byzantine army the concept of the shock cavalry charge, a tactic foreign to the Empire's forces up until this time. Many times found to be untrustworthy especially when the Empire fought against Catholic states, but they were one of the most reliable against Muslim enemies. In Byzantine service, they often adopted armour and weapon styles from the Roman armoury.
{Latinikon}	Latinikon
{Mourtatoi_descr_short}	Turkoman archers armed with composite bows and swords.
{Mourtatoi_descr}	(Μουρτάτοι).\n\nQualité : Supérieure.\nType : Local (manque d'entraînement, faible discipline et moral bas).\n\nThe Empire almost always suffered from a serious lack of good and experienced archers. The Komneneans were lucky enough to have at their disposal the sons of some of the Turkish/Turkoman settlers within the Empire’s provinces. This gave them the opportunity to revive the "kursores-defensores" type of infantry units, armed with good composite bows, round shields and swords.
{Mourtatoi}	Mourtatoi
{Pronoiarii}	Pronoiarii
{Pronoiarii_descr_short}	Wealthy Byzantine landowners who can afford the best quality weapons and armour.
{Pronoiarii_descr}	(Προνοιαριοι).\n\nQualité : Elite.\nType : Féodal (faible disponibilité, entretien nul dans les châteaux).\n\nContact with western European knights forced the Empire to equip their cavalry with heavier armour and stronger horses. To implement such a reform, the Emperor gave nobles larger tracts of land to farm (pronoiae), like those that the Scholarii had received. This system started to resemble the western European concept of feudalism. Pronoiars had the right to recruit armed squires with the obligation to join the Imperial armies in a time of danger. Some Pronoiars owned huge amounts of land and could afford large private armies, which sometimes fought against the Empire itself.
{Scholarii}	Scholarii
{Scholarii_descr_short}	Elite, heavily armoured cavalry armed with a heavy spear and amace.
{Scholarii_descr}	(Σχολάριοι).\n\nQualité : Elite.\nType : Professionnel urbain (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nThese fully professional troops, also known as cataphractoi or clivanophoroi (named for their armour), are the elite core of the imperial army. They were also known as vasilika tagmata ton ippeon or simply Tagmata. Scholarii were some of the heaviest armoured cavalry in history.
{Scoutatoi}	Scoutatoi
{Scoutatoi_descr_short}	Line infantry armed with a large shield and heavy spear.
{Scoutatoi_descr}	(Σκουτάτοι).\n\nQualité : Supérieure.\nType : Professionnel de période avancée (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nGreek and Roman units often took their names from the equipment they carried (e.g. hoplite is derived from the hoplon shield). In the Roman army the shield was known as a scutus. In the Byzantine armies, the troops who carried shields were known as Scoutatoi. These were the standard line infantry of medieval Roman armies and in addition to their large shield, they were also armed with spears and/or swords.
{Scoutatoi_Swordsmen}	Scoutatoi Swordsmen
{Scoutatoi_Swordsmen_descr_short}	Line infantry armed with a large shield and sword.
{Scoutatoi_Swordsmen_descr}	(Σκουτάτοι).\n\nQualité : Supérieure.\nType : Professionnel de période avancée (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nGreek and Roman units often took their names from the equipment they carried (e.g. hoplite is derived from the hoplon shield). In the Roman army the shield was known as a scutus. In the Byzantine armies, the troops who carried shields were known as Scoutatoi. These were the standard line infantry of medieval Roman armies and in addition to their large shield, they were also armed with spears and/or swords.
{Siphonatores}	Siphonatores
{Siphonatores_descr_short}	Heavily armoured troops wielding a hand-held siphon that shoots forth a jet of liquid flame.
{Siphonatores_descr}	(Σιφωνάτορες) Very few things are known about these Imperial troops. They were among the most trusted and loyal troops because of the secret weapon they wielded. It is known that they started as ship assault troops but that they soon were also used to defend and attack defensive walls. Their primary weapon was a hand-held version of the naval siphon that spewed forth a jet of lethal flame. Anyone caught in the path of the fire would suffer the worst burns to their body, not just because of the heat of the flame but because the greek fire would stick to their skin and clothing and continue to burn after the siphon finished firing. To help protect their secret weapon, Emperors would ensure that these troops were well protected in heavy armour.
{Spartharii_tou_Vasileos}	Spartharii tou Vasileos
{Spartharii_tou_Vasileos_descr_short}	Heavily armoured elite infantry. The personal guard of the Emperor.
{Spartharii_tou_Vasileos_descr}	(Σπαθάριοι του Βασιλέως).\n\nQualité : Exceptionnelle.\nType : Professionnel urbain (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nAfter Excubitors lost their dutyas Imperial guards and became one of the four Imperial elite units known as the Vasilica Tagmata, the personal guard of the Emperor was a small, mostly traditional unit called the Spatharioi. Their leading officer was known as Protospatharios tou vasileos and he carried the Emperor's sword in official presentations and ceremonies. The Spartharii had the Imperial armoury at their disposal, and hence they were one of the most heavily armoured units in the medieval world. However, many times the Spartharii seemed to be more loyal to the palace rather than the Emperor himself.
{Stratiotae}	Stratiotae
{Stratiotae_descr_short}	Professional cavalry armed with heavy spears, swords and shields.
{Stratiotae_descr}	(Στρατιώται).\n\nQualité : Moyenne.\nType : Professionnel de période avancée (entraînement plus long basé sur le type d'unité et la qualité, plus grande proportion d'unités disciplinées).\n\nThe cost of a soldier’s armour, weapons and horse as well as the time requirements for full military service forced the Empire to increase the size of the military farms (known as “mikrae pronoiae”) as payment These troops were the majority of the troops in any medieval Roman army. While armed with heavy spears, swords and good quality armour, Stratiotae were not shock assault cavalry like western European knights. Instead, they were mostly used as mobile strategic troops, used to attack an enemy’s flank and rear.
{Toxotae}	Toxotae

{Toxotae_descr}	(Τοξόται).\n\nQualité : Milice.\nType : Milice urbaine (entretien nul dans les villes, moral réduit dans sur les champs de bataille).\n\nAccording to the standard military manuals of the time, each provincial ruler in the Empire had to keep a certain number of militia armed as archers to defend the province’s cities. As they are merely peasants, they are not armed with more powerful composite bows, so the damage they can inflict is limited compared to other archers in the Empire’s armies. In order to improve their survivability on the battlefield, some local rulers provide padded armour to their Toxotae, in addition to the standard bow, hand axe and small buckler.

{Skythikoi}	Skythikon

{Skythikoi_descr}	(Σκυθικόν).\n\nQualité : Supérieure.\nType : Mercenaire (entretien élevé, moral et discipline souvent légèrement réduits).\n\nMedieval Romans called all warriors that came from the steppe “Skythae”. The lack of experienced mounted archers forced the Empire to hire large numbers of these warriors to counter the superior mounted archery skills of it’s enemies. These warriors came from numerous steppe tribes including Pechenegs, Cumans and Turkomans. Skythikoi were paid either by annual payments known as rogae, or they were given a proportion of all spoils won in battle.
